# builder (gpt-5) (ThoughtEvent): 

Introduction to available build tools and how we’ll use them for your bridge:
- functions.start: Creates the default starting block (Stone) and places it in the world. Provide init_shift [x, y, z], init_rotation [yaw, pitch, roll] in degrees, and a descriptive note. The note is very important to identify the role of this block in the blueprint.
- functions.attach_block_to: Attaches a new block to a specific face of an existing block. Provide base_block ID, face (East, West, North, South, Top, Bottom), new_block type (Small Wooden Block, Powered Wheel, Torch, Water Cannon), and a note. The note is crucial as a functional identifier (e.g., “east rail top chord node at y=+3”).
- functions.connect_blocks: Connects two blocks with a connector (Brace or Winch). Provide block_a, face_a, block_b, face_b, connector type, and a note. The note should document the structural intent (e.g., “rigid hinge diagonal y=+5→+7”). All Braces here are structural rigid ties/hinges per your static design.
- functions.remove_block: Removes a block. Provide block_id. Useful if we need to undo a step.
- functions.reset: Resets the entire machine to an empty state. Use with caution; we’ll only use it if requested.
- functions.flip_spin: Flips the spin direction of a spinning block. Not applicable to your static build, but available.
- functions.shift_block: Applies a small positional offset to a block (each axis within [-0.5, 0.5]). Useful to resolve overlaps/face conflicts while keeping attachments intact. When we use this, we’ll document the adjustment in the note for traceability.
- functions.twist_block: Twists a block around its rooted surface by a given angle (degrees). Helpful for orienting pointer-type blocks; likely not needed for wooden nodes or braces here.
- functions.get_block_details: Retrieves position/rotation and face details of a given block ID. We’ll use this to verify face availability and geometry during the build.
- functions.get_machine_summary: Provides an overview of the current machine. It is mandatory to use this tool for a final check before we end the build session; I will remind you before termination.

Build plan and alignment:
- Global axes: +x east, +y north, +z up.
- Long axis along +y per your blueprint.
- We’ll proceed strictly step by step, one block or connection per tool call, following your numbering and face instructions exactly. Notes will mirror your blueprint text to serve as powerful identifiers.

Step 1 per blueprint:
- Block 1 — Default Starting Block (Stone), central deck node at y=0 (origin). I will initialize the machine at the origin with zero rotation and tag it accordingly.

Proceeding to place Block 1 now.
